          </th>
          <td>
           10
          </td>
         </tr>

     <p>
      <b>
       Qingdao
      </b>
      (
      <span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Mandarin" title="Help:IPA for Mandarin">
        [tit]
       </a>
      </span>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">
       Chinese
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="zh-Hans">
       
      </span>
      ; formerly
      <b>
       Tsingtao
      </b>
      ) is a city in eastern
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shandong_Province" title="Shandong Province">
       Shandong Province
      </a>
      on the east coast of
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      . Administered at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city" title="Sub-provincial city">
       sub-provincial level
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Qingdao has jurisdiction over seven districts and five county-level cities. According to the
      <a href="/wiki/Sixth_National_Population_Census_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sixth National Population Census of the People's Republic of China">
       2010 census
      </a>
      , the built-up (
      <i>
       or metro
      </i>
      ) area made up of 6 urban districts and Jimo City had 5,764,384 inhabitants,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while the total population of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city" title="Sub-provincial city">
       sub-provincial city
      </a>
      is up to 8.71 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2010_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Census2010-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Lying across the
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Peninsula" title="Shandong Peninsula">
       Shandong Peninsula
      </a>
      and looking out to the
      <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">
       Yellow Sea
      </a>
      , it borders
      <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">
       Yantai
      </a>
      to the northeast,
      <a href="/wiki/Weifang" title="Weifang">
       Weifang
      </a>
      to the west and
      <a href="/wiki/Rizhao" title="Rizhao">
       Rizhao
      </a>
      to the southwest.
      <i>
       Qng
      </i>
      (
      <span lang="zh">
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%9D%92" title="wikt:">
        
       </a>
      </span>
      ) in Chinese means "green" or "lush", while
      <i>
       do
      </i>
      (
      <span lang="zh">
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B2%9B" title="wikt:">
        
       </a>
      </span>
      ) means "island".
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao is a major
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">
       seaport
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Naval_base" title="Naval base">
       naval base
      </a>
      , and industrial centre. The world's longest sea bridge, the
      <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay_Bridge" title="Jiaozhou Bay Bridge">
       Jiaozhou Bay Bridge
      </a>
      , links the main urban area of Qingdao with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huangdao" title="Huangdao">
       Huangdao
      </a>
      district, straddling the
      <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay" title="Jiaozhou Bay">
       Jiaozhou Bay
      </a>
      sea areas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also the site of the
      <a href="/wiki/Tsingtao_Brewery" title="Tsingtao Brewery">
       Tsingtao Brewery
      </a>
      , the second largest brewery in China.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2007, Qingdao was named as among China's top ten cities by the Chinese Cities Brand Value Report, which was released at the 2007 Beijing Summit of China Cities Forum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2009, Qingdao was named China's most livable city by the Chinese Institute of City Competitiveness.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32">
          <a href="#Western_part_of_Shinan_district_.28.E5.B8.82.E5.8D.97.E5.8C.BA.E8.A5.BF.E9.83.A8.29">

           </span>

           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33">
          <a href="#Eastern_part_of_Shinan_district_.28.E5.B8.82.E5.8D.97.E5.8C.BA.E4.B8.9C.E9.83.A8.29">

           <span class="tocnumber">
            11.3
           </span>

           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35">
          <a href="#Other_districts_of_Qingdao">

         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36">
        <a href="#Education">

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_names">
       Other names
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Other names">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        Jio'o
       </b>
       : (
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%83%B6" title="wikt:">
        
       </a>
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%BE%B3" title="wikt:">
        
       </a>
       ): former name during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">
        Qing Dynasty
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Qindao
       </b>
       : (
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%90%B4" title="wikt:">
        
       </a>
       , lit. "Stringed Instrument Isle"): additional modern name for the area, refers according to locals to the shape of the coastline.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Tsingtao
       </b>
       :
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Postal_Map_Romanisation" title="Chinese Postal Map Romanisation">
        Chinese Postal Map Romanisation
       </a>
       spelling
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Tsingtau
       </b>
       : German name during the concession period, written in German romanization of Chinese (
       <a href="/wiki/Lessing-Othmer" title="Lessing-Othmer">
        Lessing-Othmer
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Jiaozhou
       </b>
       : a historical name which refers to the
       <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay" title="Jiaozhou Bay">
        Jiaozhou Bay
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Kiaochow
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Kiauchau
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Kiautschou
       </b>
       : romanizations of Jiaozhou.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_times">
       Ancient times
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient times">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Human settlement in the area dates back 6,000 years. The
      <a href="/wiki/Dongyi" title="Dongyi">
       Dongyi
      </a>
      nationality, one of the important origins of the Chinese nation, lived here and created the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dawenkou" title="Dawenkou">
       Dawenkou
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Longshan_culture" title="Longshan culture">
       Longshan
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dongyeshi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dongyeshi (page does not exist)">
       Dongyeshi
      </a>
      cultures. In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Zhou_Dynasty" title="Eastern Zhou Dynasty">
       Eastern Zhou Dynasty
      </a>
      (770BC~256BC), the town of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jimo,_Shandong" title="Jimo, Shandong">
       Jimo
      </a>
      was established, which was then the second largest one in the Shandong region. The area in which Qingdao is located today was named Jiao'ao () when it was administered by the Qing Dynasty on 14 June 1891.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="German_colonial_period_and_Japanese_occupations">
       German colonial period and Japanese occupations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German colonial period and Japanese occupations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qingdao-map-1906.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="977" data-file-width="1536" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Qingdao-map-1906.jpg/220px-Qingdao-map-1906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Qingdao-map-1906.jpg/330px-Qingdao-map-1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Qingdao-map-1906.jpg/440px-Qingdao-map-1906.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qingdao-map-1906.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sketch map of Tsingtao, circa 1906
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01,_Tsingtau,_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="800" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01%2C_Tsingtau%2C_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-125-01,_Tsingtau,_Haupttor_des_Artillerielagers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Main gate of Chinese munitions depot, taken over by imperial navy, 1898
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127,_China,_Tsingtau.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="513" data-file-width="798" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127%2C_China%2C_Tsingtau.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_116-424-127,_China,_Tsingtau.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Administration/commercial building, harbor area, 1912
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For more details on this topic, see
      <a href="/wiki/Kiautschou_Bay_concession" title="Kiautschou Bay concession">
       Kiautschou Bay concession
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1891, the Qing government decided to make the area a defense base against naval attack and began to improve Qingdao's existing fortifications. German naval officials observed and reported on this Chinese activity during a formal survey of
      <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay" title="Jiaozhou Bay">
       Jiaozhou Bay
      </a>
      in May 1897. Subsequently, German troops seized and occupied the fortification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      China conceded the area to Germany the following year, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Kiautschou_Bay_concession" title="Kiautschou Bay concession">
       Kiautschou Bay concession
      </a>
      , as it became known, existed from 1898 to 1914. With an area of 552 square kilometres (136,000 acres; 213sqmi), it was located in the imperial province of
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">
       Shandong
      </a>
      (alternately romanized as Shantung or Shan-tung) on the southern coast of the Shandong Peninsula in northern China. Jiaozhou was romanized as Kiaochow, Kiauchau or Kiao-Chau in English and Kiautschou in German. Qingdao was its administrative center. "The so-called
      <i>
       Marktstrasse
      </i>
      (Market street) was nothing more than the old main street of the Chinese village of Tsingtao, and the buildings lining it were the former homes of fishermen and farmers. Having sold their property, they resettled their homes and fields in the villages further east."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matzat1_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Matzat1-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Upon gaining control of the area, the Germans outfitted the impoverished fishing village of "Tsingtao" (Qingdao) with wide streets, solid housing areas, government buildings, electrification throughout, a sewer system and a safe drinking water supply, a rarity in large parts of Asia at that time and later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flagge_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Flagge-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The area had the highest school density and the highest
      <i>
       per capita
      </i>
      student enrollment in all of China, with primary, secondary and vocational schools funded by the
      <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
       Imperial German
      </a>
      treasury and Protestant and Roman Catholic missions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flagge_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Flagge-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Commercial interests established the Germania Brewery in 1903, which later became the world-famous
      <a href="/wiki/Tsingtao_Brewery" title="Tsingtao Brewery">
       Tsingtao Brewery
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matzat2_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Matzat2-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      German influence extended to other areas of Shandong Province, including the establishment of diverse commercial enterprises.
     </p>
     <p>
      Identified by the German authorities as a strategically important port, Qingdao was administered by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reichsmarineamt" title="Reichsmarineamt">
       Imperial Department of the Navy
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Reichsmarineamt
      </i>
      ) rather than the
      <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Colonial_Office" title="Imperial Colonial Office">
       Imperial Colonial Office
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Reichskolonialamt
      </i>
      ). The navy based their
      <a href="/wiki/German_East_Asia_Squadron" title="German East Asia Squadron">
       Far East Squadron
      </a>
      there, allowing the ships to conduct operations throughout the Pacific. Beginning January 1898 the marines of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Seebataillon" title="Seebataillon">
        III. Seebataillon
       </a>
      </i>
      were based at Tsingtao. Construction of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiaoji_Railway" title="Jiaoji Railway">
       Jiaoji Railway
      </a>
      began on September 23, 1899, and was completed in 1904.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Before the outbreak of World War I, ships of the German naval forces under
      <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_von_Spee" title="Maximilian von Spee">
       Admiral Count von Spee
      </a>
      were located at central Pacific colonies on routine missions. The fleet then rendezvoused in the Marianas to plan a transit to Germany rather than be trapped in the Pacific by Allied fleets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After a minor British naval attack on the German colony in 1914, Japan occupied the city and the surrounding province during the
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tsingtao" title="Siege of Tsingtao">
       Siege of Tsingtao
      </a>
      after Japan's declaration of war on Germany in accordance with the
      <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Japanese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Japanese Alliance">
       Anglo-Japanese Alliance
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Source_Records_of_the_Great_War.2C_Vol._III.2C_ed._Charles_F._Horne.2C_National_Alumni_1923_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Source_Records_of_the_Great_War.2C_Vol._III.2C_ed._Charles_F._Horne.2C_National_Alumni_1923-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      China protested Japan's violation of her neutrality but did not interfere in the operations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The failure of the Allied powers to restore Chinese rule to Shandong after the war triggered the
      <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">
       May Fourth Movement
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1184" data-file-width="1585" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png/220px-Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png/330px-Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png/440px-Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Image-Qingdao_city_map_1912_in_german.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of Qingdao in 1912
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The city reverted to Chinese rule in December, 1922, under control of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">
       Republic of China
      </a>
      . However, Japan maintained its economic dominance of the railway and the province as a whole.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city became a
      <a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality" title="Direct-controlled municipality">
       direct-controlled municipality
      </a>
      of the ROC Government in 1929. Japan re-occupied Qingdao in 1938 with its plans of territorial expansion into China's coast.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Qingdao_city_planning_and_development">
       Qingdao city planning and development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Qingdao city planning and development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1891, the Qing Government decided to make coastal Tsingtao (Jiao'ao) a defense base against naval attack and started the spade work of improving its existing fortifications. However, Tsingtao was taken over in November 1891 by German troops on the excuse of the murder in the region of a German missionary, which led to the signing, on March 6, 1898, of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kiautschou_Bay_concession" title="Kiautschou Bay concession">
       Kiautschou Bay concession
      </a>
      Treaty between the Qing Dynasty and Germany and the interruption of Chinese endeavors of local urban construction (Li 2005, p.81). From then on, Tsingtao had been a German colony until November 1914, when the Japanese took the place of Germany.
     </p>
     <p>
      After the First World War, the Chinese people struggled for the return of Tsingtao, which in 1919 triggered the well-known 
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/May_4th_Movement" title="May 4th Movement">
       May 4th Movement
      </a>
       in connection with Tsingtao sovereignty. On February 4, 1922, Japan could do nothing but sign with the Chinese Government the Sino- Japanese Treaty. China took back Tsingtao on December 10 the same year and opened it up to commerce and trade. The city became a directly-controlled municipality of the Republic of China (ROC) in July 1929. Nevertheless, Tsingtao fell into the hands of the Japanese once again in January 1938 and was taken back once again in September 1945. The city was occupied by Chairman Mao Zedong and his troops on June 2, 1949, shortly before the founding of the Peoples Republic of China on October 1, 1949.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1891.E2.80.931914">
       18911914
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 18911914">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The development of Tsingtao urban space during Germany-occupied period (18911914). The urban development of Tsingtao originated from the port area in the southern since the occupation by Germany in 1891. The large scale urban construction began in 1898 with the relocation of Chinese dwellers along the coast.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With the completion of such series of projects as wharves, Tsingtao-Jinan Railway Line,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tsingtao Railway Station and locomotive works, a city was starting to take shape. The area had the highest schools density and highest per capita student enrollment in all of China, with primary, secondary and vocational schools funded by the Berlin treasury and Protestant and Roman Catholic missions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the year of 1910, the Germans drew up for the second time the city planning of Tsingtao (Warner 2001, p.33). As a result, the former urban area was extended for four times highlighted by the emphasis on the development of commerce and trade.
      <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">
       Sun Yat-sen
      </a>
      visited the Tsingtau area and stated in 1912, ... I am impressed. The city is a true model for Chinas future.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1914.E2.80.931922">
       19141922
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 19141922">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The development of Tsingtao urban space during the first Japan-occupied period (19141922). In 1914, Tsingtao was taken over by Japanese and served as a base for the plunder of natural resources of Shandong and the North of China. With the development of industry and commerce, a so-called New City District was established to furnish the Japanese colonists with commercial sections and living quarters, which suggested a striking contrast to the shabby houses in the local Chinese zones(Li 2007, p.133). In the meantime, a number of schools, hospitals and public buildings were constructed, followed by urban streets and intercity highways as well. The urban spatial layout continued to expand northward along the eastern bay area.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1922.E2.80.931938">
       19221938
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19221938">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The development of Tsingtao urban space during the ROC-ruled period (19221938). This period saw the substantial progress of the urban development of Tsingtao. The government engaged itself in mass construction that gave birth to villa districts at the beach and bank groups in CBD. Plenty of public buildings and facilities for the purpose of entertainment and sports were completed. By the year of 1937, the urban population numbered 385,000(Lu 2001, p.327). Tsingtao consequently distinguished itself as a prominent holiday resort and summer retreat.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1938.E2.80.931945">
       19381945
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 19381945">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The development of Tsingtao urban space during the second Japan-occupied period (19381945). Japan staged a comeback to Tsingtao in 1938 and started to strive for the construction of the Greater Tsingtao in the following June. Accordingly, they worked out the City Planning of the Greater Tsingtao and the City Planning of the Mother Town (Tsingtao City Proper), even though they had not had the opportunity to realize them respectively. The period in question did not witness much urban progress except for the logical construction of No. 6 Wharf, some Japanese residences and a small number of roads and streets(Lu 2001, p.339).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Post.E2.80.93World_War_II">
       PostWorld War II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: PostWorld War II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      After World War II the
      <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">
       KMT
      </a>
      allowed Qingdao to serve as the headquarters of the Western Pacific Fleet of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Navy" title="US Navy">
       US Navy
      </a>
      in 1945. On 2 June 1949, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">
       CCP
      </a>
      -led
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Red_Army" title="Chinese Red Army">
       Red Army
      </a>
      entered Qingdao and the city and province have been under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
       PRC
      </a>
      control since that time.
     </p>
     <p>
      Since the 1984 inauguration of China's open-door policy to foreign trade and investment, western Qingdao developed quickly as a port city. It is now the headquarters of the Chinese navy's northern fleet. An early example of the open-door policy occurred on 5 November 1984, when three United States Naval vessels visited Qingdao. This was the first US port call in more than 37 years to China.
      <a href="/wiki/USS_Rentz_(FFG-46)" title="USS Rentz (FFG-46)">
       USS
       <i>
        Rentz
       </i>
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/USS_Reeves_(DLG-24)" title="USS Reeves (DLG-24)">
       USS
       <i>
        Reeves
       </i>
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/USS_Oldendorf_(DD-972)" title="USS Oldendorf (DD-972)">
       USS
       <i>
        Oldendorf
       </i>
      </a>
      and their crews were officially hosted by the Chinese
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Navy" title="People's Liberation Army Navy">
       People's Liberation Army Navy
      </a>
      (PLAN).
     </p>
     <p>
      Northern Qingdao, particularly
      <a href="/wiki/Shibei_District" title="Shibei District">
       Shibei
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Licang_District" title="Licang District">
       Licang
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Chengyang_District" title="Chengyang District">
       Chengyang
      </a>
      districts, are now major manufacturing centers. The city has recently experienced a strong growth period, with a new central business district created to the east of the older business district. Outside of the center of the city, there is a large industrial zone, which includes chemical processing, rubber and heavy manufacturing, in addition to a growing high-tech area. Numerous local and national service companies, rather than manufacturers, are based in the city's southern district; this, as well as local wind patterns, allows Qingdao to enjoy clean, clear air year round.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">

      (

      </i>
      ):
     </p>

     <p>
      Qingdao is located on the south facing coast of the
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Peninsula" title="Shandong Peninsula">
       Shandong Peninsula
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
       German
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="de">
       <i>
        Schantung-Halbinsel
       </i>
      </span>
      ). It borders three prefecture-level cities, namely
      <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">
       Yantai
      </a>
      to the northeast,
      <a href="/wiki/Weifang" title="Weifang">
       Weifang
      </a>
      to the west, and
      <a href="/wiki/Rizhao" title="Rizhao">
       Rizhao
      </a>
      to the southwest. The city's total jurisdiction area occupies 10,654 square kilometres (4,114sqmi), and stretches in latitude from 35 35' to 37 09' N and in longitude from 119 30' to 121 00' E. The populated sections of the city are relatively flat while mountains spur up within city limits and nearby. The highest elevation in the city is 1,133 metres (3,717ft)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
       above sea level
      </a>
      . Of the total area of Qingdao, 15.5% is highland, while the foothill, plain and lowland areas constitute 25.1%, 37.8% and 21.7%. The city has a 730.64 kilometres (454.00mi) coastline. Five significant rivers that flow for more than 50 kilometres (31mi) can be found in the region.
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao has a temperate, four-season,
      <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">
       monsoon
      </a>
      -influenced
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDIO_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SDIO-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      climate that lies in the transition between the
      <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
       humid subtropical
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Kppen climate classification">
       Kppen
      </a>
      <i>
       Cwa
      </i>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
       humid continental
      </a>
      (Kppen
      <i>
       Dwa
      </i>
      ) regimes, but favouring the former. Winter is cool to cold and windy, but generally dry, with a January average of 0.5C (31.1F). Summer is generally hot and humid, but very hot days are rare, with an August average of 25.3C (77.5F). Due to its proximity to the coast and being on a peninsula, it experiences a one-month delayed spring compared to most inland areas of China,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDIO_24-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SDIO-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the annual
      <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">
       diurnal temperature variation
      </a>
      is only 6.3C (11.3F). Conversely, autumn is milder than inland areas in Shandong. The water temperature peaks at about 25C (77F) in late August, with swimming possible two months on either side. The annual mean temperature is 12.6C (54.7F).
     </p>
     <p>
      During the summer months, the beaches of Qingdao are afflicted by massive
      <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">
       algal blooms
      </a>
      . The decomposing algae release large amounts of
      <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">
       hydrogen sulfide
      </a>
      gas, which gives off the odour of rotten eggs. The blooms of
      <a href="/wiki/Sea_lettuce" title="Sea lettuce">
       sea lettuce
      </a>
      , which are partially caused by seaweed farming in Jiangsu Province, led local officials to declare a "large-scale algae disaster" in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">
      <tr>
       <th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">

       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      By the end of 2006, Qingdao was estimated to be the home of about 8 million inhabitants, of which around 3 million reside in the Qingdao urban area. Another estimated 5 million live in other cities under Qingdao's jurisdiction. The annual birth rate is calculated around 76,507, with a
      <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">
       birth rate
      </a>
      of 10.15 per year per thousand, and a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_rate" title="Death rate">
       death rate
      </a>
      of 6.32, both calculated on an annual basis. Living standards are among the highest of leading Chinese cities due to the strong export economy and relatively high family wages.
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao is home to 38
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalities" title="Chinese nationalities">
       Chinese ethnic minorities
      </a>
      , which account for 0.14% of the city's total population.
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a large Korean community in Qingdao. By 2009, there are approximately 100,000 Koreans working, studying and living in Qingdao, which makes Qingdao the second in terms of Korean population in China, following Beijing which has about 200,000 Koreans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1333" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg/170px-Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg/255px-Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg/340px-Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Views_of_Qingdao_tower.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Qingdao TV Tower
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      An important region in Eastern China, Shandong Province has seen substantial change in its economic landscape in recent years. Much of this development has been concentrated in Qingdao.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KPMG_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-KPMG-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Qingdao has seen rapid development. With an annual growth rate of 18.9 percent in 2006, the city's GDP reached 42.3 billion, ranking first in Shandong Province and tenth out of China's top 20 cities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KPMG_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-KPMG-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
       GDP
      </a>
      per capita comprised
      <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">
       RMB
      </a>
      52,895 (US$7,616) in 2008. The GDP has grown steadily at an average pace of 16% annually. In 2006, Qingdao was ranked one of six "golden cities" by the World Bank, out of 120 Chinese cities assessed on factors including investment climate and government effectiveness.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KPMG_28-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-KPMG-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Internationally, Qingdao is perhaps best known for its
      <a href="/wiki/Tsingtao_Brewery" title="Tsingtao Brewery">
       Tsingtao Brewery
      </a>
      , founded by a German-British joint venture in 1903 that produces
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsingtao_beer" title="Tsingtao beer">
       Tsingtao beer
      </a>
      , the best-known Chinese export beer. It is also home to
      <a href="/wiki/Haier" title="Haier">
       Haier
      </a>
      , a large
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_goods" title="White goods">
       white goods
      </a>
      manufacturer, and
      <a href="/wiki/Hisense" title="Hisense">
       Hisense
      </a>
      , a major electronics company. In 2002 guitar manufacturers
      <a href="/wiki/Epiphone" title="Epiphone">
       Epiphone
      </a>
      opened a factory in Qingdao.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1984 the Chinese government named a district of Qingdao a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of the People's Republic of China">
       Special Economic and Technology Development Zone
      </a>
      (SETDZ). Along with this district, the entire city had gone through amazing development of secondary and tertiary industries. As an important trading port in the province, Qingdao flourishes with foreign investment and international trade.
      <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">
       South Korea
      </a>
      and Japan in particular made extensive investment in the city. Approximately 80,000 South Korean citizens reside there. Construction proceeds at a relatively fast pace in Qingdao.
     </p>
     <p>
      In terms of primary industry, Qingdao has an estimated 50,000 acres (200km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) of
      <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">
       arable land
      </a>
      . Qingdao has a zigzagging pattern coastline, and thus possesses an invaluable stock of fish,
      <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">
       shrimp
      </a>
      , and other sea resources.
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao is also home to a variety of mineral resources. Up to thirty different kinds have been mined.
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao's
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">
       wind power
      </a>
      electricity generation performs at among the highest levels in the region.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_zones">
       Industrial zones
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Industrial zones">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Qingdao Special Economic &amp; Technological Development Area
      </li>
      <li>
       Qingdao Free Trade Zone
      </li>
      <li>
       Qingdao High-tech Industrial Zone
      </li>
      <li>
       Qingdao University Industrial Zone
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
       Transport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Road">
       Road
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Road">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The total lengths of operational highways
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2013)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      is 14,326km (8,902mi), including 700km (430mi) Expressways. At the present,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
         <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2013)">
          when?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      the traffic mileage is more than 6.02billion km (3.74billionmi) per year.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      There are a total of 1,145km (711mi) of roads in the Qingdao area, with nearly 500km (310mi) of expressways. These
      <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_China" title="Expressways of China">
       National Trunk Highway System (NTHS)
      </a>
      Expressways begin or pass through in Qingdao.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Expressways that beigin in Qingdao are in
      <b>
       Bold
      </b>
      :
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       G15
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenhai_Expressway" title="Shenhai Expressway">
        Shenhai Expressway
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">
        Shenyang
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">
        Liaoning
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Haikou" title="Haikou">

       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">

       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       G18
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rongwu_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rongwu Expressway (page does not exist)">

       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Rongcheng,_Shandong" title="Rongcheng, Shandong">

       </a>
       , Shandong-
       <a href="/wiki/Wuhai" title="Wuhai">
        Wuhai
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">
        Inner Mongolia
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        G20
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qingyin_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qingyin Expressway (page does not exist)">
         Qingyin Expressway
        </a>
       </b>
       (Qingdao-
       <a href="/wiki/Yinchuan" title="Yinchuan">

       <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">

       </a>
       )
      </li>

     <p>
      Spur Route:
      <b>
       G2011
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qingxin_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qingxin Expressway (page does not exist)">
        Qingxin Expressway
       </a>
      </b>
      (Qingdao-
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhe,_Shandong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xinhe, Shandong (page does not exist)">

      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pingdu" title="Pingdu">
       Pingdu
      </a>
      , Shandong)
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        G22
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qinglan_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qinglan Expressway (page does not exist)">

        </a>
       </b>
       (Qingdao-
       <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">

        Gansu
       </a>
       )
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      These provincial expressways begin in or pass through Qingdao. Expressways that begin in Qingdao are in
      <b>
       Bold
      </b>
      :
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       S16
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rongwei_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rongwei Expressway (page does not exist)">

       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Rongcheng,_Shandong" title="Rongcheng, Shandong">

       )

      <li>

        </a>
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Longkou" title="Longkou">
        Longkou
       </a>
       -Qingdao)
      </li>
      <li>
       S21
       <b>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xinwei_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xinwei Expressway (page does not exist)">
         Xinwei Expressway
        </a>
       </b>
       (
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xinhe,_Shandong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xinhe, Shandong (page does not exist)">

     <p>
      Other than Expressways, there are also
      <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highways" title="China National Highways">
       National Highways
      </a>
      that pass through or begin in Qingdao. National Highways that begin in Qingdao are in
      <b>
       bold
      </b>
      :
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_204" title="China National Highway 204">
        G204
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">
        Yantai
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
        Shanghai
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_206" title="China National Highway 206">
        G206
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">
        Yantai
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">
        Shantou
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_308" title="China National Highway 308">
         G308
        </a>
       </b>
       (Qingdao-
       <a href="/wiki/Shijiazhuang" title="Shijiazhuang">
        Shijiazhuang
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_309" title="China National Highway 309">
        G309
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Rongcheng,_Shandong" title="Rongcheng, Shandong">
        Rongcheng
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">
        Lanzhou
       </a>
       )
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      In June 30, 2011, the longest bridge over water opened in Qingdao. The bridge,
      <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay_Bridge" title="Jiaozhou Bay Bridge">
       Haiwan Bridge
      </a>
      , is 26.4 miles (42.5km) long and connects Qingdao to an offshore island, Huangdao. It would easily cross the English Channel and is almost three miles (4.8km) longer than the previous record-holder, the Lake Pontchartrain Causeway in the American state of Louisiana. Haiwan Bridge is supported by more than 5,000 pillars and costs about 10 billion yuan which is about 1.5 billion dollars. The bridge was designed by the Shandong Gausu Group and the construction lasted for four years. Haiwan Bridge cut the commute between the city of Qingdao and the sprawling suburb of Huangdao by 30 minutes. At least 10,000 workers toiled in two teams around the clock to build the bridge, which was constructed from opposite ends.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the same day, the
      <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_Jiaozhou_Bay_tunnel" title="Qingdao Jiaozhou Bay tunnel">
       Jiaozhou Bay Tunnel
      </a>
      opened.The tunnel brought much convenience to people by supporting public buses and making transport between the two areas more convenient.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Marine">
       Marine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Marine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       Orient Ferry
      </i>
      connects Qingdao with
      <a href="/wiki/Shimonoseki" title="Shimonoseki">
       Shimonoseki
      </a>
      , Japan. There are two ferry lines connecting Qingdao with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Korea" title="Republic of Korea">
       South Korea
      </a>
      . The
      <i>
       New Golden Bridge II
      </i>
      operates between Qingdao and
      <a href="/wiki/Incheon" title="Incheon">
       Incheon
      </a>
      , and the
      <i>
       Blue Sea Ferry
      </i>
      operates between Qingdao and
      <a href="/wiki/Gunsan" title="Gunsan">
       Gunsan
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Qingdao hosts one of the world's busiest
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_of_Qingdao" title="Port of Qingdao">
       seaports
      </a>
      . Cooperative relations have been established with 450 ports in 130 countries worldwide. In 2003, the annual cargo handling capacity exceeded 100 million
      <a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">
       tons
      </a>
      for the first time. The number of containers reached 3.41 million
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">
       twenty-foot equivalent units
      </a>
      (TEU) of cargoes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 2011, the port had become the worlds sixth-busiest by Total Cargo Volume, having handled 372 million tonnes of cargo in that year. It is the 8th in the world in terms of TEUs (Twenty Foot Equivalent Units).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">
       Aviation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aviation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_Liuting_International_Airport" title="Qingdao Liuting International Airport">
       Qingdao Liuting International Airport
      </a>
      , 23km (14mi) away from city centre, is served by 13 domestic and international
      <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">
       airlines
      </a>
      , operating 94 routes, 12 of which are international and regional. In 2011, Qingdao Liuting International Airport was the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="List of the busiest airports in the People's Republic of China">
       16th busiest
      </a>
      airport in the People's Republic of China with 11,716,361 passengers. A new civil aviation airport with much larger capacities will be built in Jiaozhou District.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_rail">
       Intercity rail
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Intercity rail">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg/220px-Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg/330px-Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg/440px-Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qingdao_Railway_Station_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Qingdao railway station
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Qingdao's railway development was picked up during the late 1990s. It is at the beginning of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiaoji_Railway" title="Jiaoji Railway">
       Jiaoji Railway
      </a>
      . Qingdao's city proper has some major railway stations,
      <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_Railway_Station" title="Qingdao Railway Station">
       Qingdao Station
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sifang_railway_station" title="Sifang railway station">
       Sifang Station
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cangkou Station, Great-Seaport Station, etc.
     </p>
     <p>
      D and G series High speed trains travel on the Jiaoji High Speed Railway and reach speeds of 200km/h (120mph) on the Jinan-Qingdao Section.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Services go to
      <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">
       Beijing
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
       Shanghai
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hefei" title="Hefei">
       Hefei
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">
       Jinan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">
       Tianjin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Domestic rail lines connect Qingdao with many cities in China including
      <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">
       Beijing
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">
       Lanzhou
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">
       Chengdu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi'an">
       Xi'an
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zhengzhou" title="Zhengzhou">
       Zhengzhou
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">
       Jinan
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jining,_Shandong" title="Jining, Shandong">
       Jining
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">
       Public transport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public transport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Qingdao's public traffic owns 5283 large and medium-sized buses,
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">
       CNG
      </a>
      buses as of 2012.There are also 136
      <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
       trolleybuses
      </a>
      as of 2012. There are 260 bus routes and 3 trolleybus routes as of 2012.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      All of these buses and trolleybuses can be accessed using the Qingdao Public Traffic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IC_Card" title="IC Card">
       IC Card
      </a>
      (Qin dao Card
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%90%B4" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B2%9B" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%8D%A1" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      ), which uses radio frequencies so the card does not have to physically touch the scanner. Non air-conditioned busses cost 1 yuan, The volume of road passenger transport approaches 0.8 billion per year.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The Public Transport Brand of 'Ri-Xin Bus (
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%97%A5" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%96%B0" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B7%B4" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%A3%AB" title="wikt:">
       
      </a>
      )' is also known in China.
     </p>
     <p>
      There are a number of taxi companies in Qingdao including Yiqing Company, Zhongqing Company, Jiaoyun Company and, Huaqing Company.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Subway">
       Subway
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Subway">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_Metro" title="Qingdao Metro">
       Qingdao Metro
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      After getting the approval from the State Council, the government announced on 18 August 2009 that Qingdao is ready to spend more than 29 billion yuan ($4.2 billion) before 2016 on its subway construction. Construction of 54.7km (34.0mi) of subway line will be completed before 2016 with a total investment of 29.2 billion yuan ($4.3 billion). Metro Line 3 will be the first line in function and is planned to open in 2014. In the long term, the city plans to build eight subway lines in downtown and some suburban districts, which account for 231.5km (143.8mi) in future.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
       Military
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Qingdao is headquarters of the
      <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Fleet" title="North Sea Fleet">
       North Sea Fleet
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Navy" title="People's Liberation Army Navy">
       People's Liberation Army Navy
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">
       Architecture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Architecture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Views_of_Qingdao.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Views_of_Qingdao.jpg/220px-Views_of_Qingdao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Views_of_Qingdao.jpg/330px-Views_of_Qingdao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Views_of_Qingdao.jpg/440px-Views_of_Qingdao.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Views_of_Qingdao.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Qingdao retains many buildings with a German architectural style
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      There is a large number of German-style buildings in Qingdao city centre, remarkable considering the German colonial period only lasted 16 years (18981914). The unique combination of German and Chinese architecture in the city centre, combined with German demographic roots and a large Korean expatriate population, gives Qingdao a distinct atmosphere. An old saying described Qingdao as a city of "red tiles green trees, blue sky and blue sea." This saying indeed gives a picture of birdview of Qingdao. A larger number of areas in former foreign styles are well preserved. Although the new city area is under large-scale reconstruction, the old city area (especially the western part of
      <a href="/wiki/Shinan_District" title="Shinan District">
       Shinan District
      </a>
      ) still retains many traditional buildings.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
       Language
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Language">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During the city's colonial days,
      <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
       German
      </a>
      was the official language and rigorously taught and promoted. Since the demise of Germany's colonial empire during World War I, the German language is virtually dead here and left little impact on the local languages. A local accent known as
      <a href="/wiki/Qingdao_dialect" title="Qingdao dialect">
       Qingdao dialect
      </a>
      (, pinyin
      <i>
       qingdao hua
      </i>
      ) distinguishes the residents of the city from those of the surrounding
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">
       Shandong
      </a>
      province. Due to the efforts by the city government to promote standard
      <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">
       Mandarin
      </a>
      , most educated people can speak that language in addition to their native language. With reform policies and English teaching, some young citizens have been taught English and many can converse with English-speaking foreigners. Business and traffic signs in English are becoming more and more common.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
       Cuisine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qingdao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Seafood is a typical delicacy of the coastal city, divided into two categories: "Great Seafood" including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_cucumber_(food)" title="Sea cucumber (food)">
       sea cucumbers
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Abalone" title="Abalone">
       abalones
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">
       shark
      </a>
      's fin,
      <a href="/wiki/Prawn" title="Prawn">
       prawns
      </a>
      , crabs,
      <a href="/wiki/Conch" title="Conch">
       conch
      </a>
      , and some big fish, and "Little Seafood" comprising
      <a href="/wiki/Squid" title="Squid">
       squid
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">
       shrimps
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Octopus" title="Octopus">
       octopus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">
       oysters
      </a>
      , razor clams,
      <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">
       clams
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Littorina" title="Littorina">
       periwinkles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yellow_croaker&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yellow croaker (page does not exist)">
       yellow croakers
      </a>
      , etc. Generally, fresh seafood is served in every hotel.
     </p>
     <p>
      The distinctive cuisine of the area is
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong_cuisine" title="Shandong cuisine">
       Lu Cai
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">
       Shandong
      </a>
      regional style.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">
       Festivals
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        ]
